Now it is 2004 and the Gore presidency is stable, if a bit rocky. Afghanistan seems to be the only thing keeping Gore afloat, but Americans want more blood shed for what happened in 2001. There are numerous people being floated as potential candidates for the Republican primaries. Senator Bond, Mayor Guilaini, and even a comeback for McCain. Whoever the person may be, they will need to do a good job at trying to take the White House.

And there remains Jeb Bush. The governor that was once the darling of people like Limbaugh is disgusted by him now. Now working in the private sector and making occasional appearances with Governor Crist at select events, maybe the time for politics is over for him. Sure he got the governor’s office, but that must not be all he wants right? What if he wanted to dip his toes back into politics again? Maybe a run for Senate in ‘04? Jeb Bush: What Could've Been In 2000

" e.pages = ["

The governorship of Jeb Bush had its ups and downs, expected for a man with political views such as him. Although initially promising an administration of strict conservatism, it would all come to a head when dealing with the legislature. Continually decrying the idea of government and getting into constant fights with them, it did not make getting his agenda passed any easier.

The prime example of Jeb’s first term as governor would be in ‘97 when he went through with his promise of restricting the protections homosexual people have in civil rights laws in the state on the ballot. While the governor would not campaign for the measure, his base and allies in the religious right would do so. Despite the money poured into supporting it, it would fail by 5% and would be indicative of the Jeb governorship thus far.

", "

It was thought that his reelection campaign was in the dirt, a good observation at the time due to Jeb’s unwillingness to compromise. That would change in ‘97 when he stated he would be willing to work with the Democrats on measures to protect Florida’s environment. Slowly but surely, Jeb would start to salvage his image and his governorship as not one of an arch-conservative, but of a common-sense conservative. While his most devoted base, especially the religious right, would be disappointed with this pivot it was necessary to even carry out the job that comes with being governor.

It would all pay off in ‘98 as Jeb would win by 6 points against his Democratic opponent Rick Danztler. The race was initially seen as very close and sometimes showing Rick ahead of him by 2 points at one point. Though as the election got close the polls would start to show Jeb in the lead, and ultimately to victory. Many attribute his victory to his new image as a ‘compassionate conservative’, and that would be how Jeb would govern for his second term.

", "

Jeb’s second term as governor would be marked as a turning point for the man. For someone that was deemed a ‘head-banging’ conservative to a much more restrained conservative than he once was. One particular event that would be emblematic of the new Jeb governorship would be of his work in rehabilitating juveniles. Once claiming that these children would need to face the full force of the law was now working towards giving these troubled children a way out of their situation. He would receive praise for this, and it seemed things were looking up for the governor.

With the name of Jeb now no longer being associated with what he was previously, a few rank-and-file members of the party saw potential in him as president. They would make nudges for him to run, but Jeb would give no comment. Whenever he was asked by a reporter if he would run, he would give vague answers. It definitely was something he toyed with but not planning on. It would all come to a head in ‘99 when at a ceremony for the preservation of the Everglades a reporter asked Jeb if he would announce his run for president. Jeb would give his comment:

“I am currently not considering it, now please no more questions at this moment thank you.”

", "

The absence of Jeb left the primaries to be anyone’s game, but one person out of the pack would make an effort to do so. John McCain would use his label as a ‘maverick’, and it would lead to a score of victories. His opponents such as Bauer and Hatch would put up a fight, and even Forbes would get in with a victory of his own. Though there would be no competition as Super Tuesday came and went and resulted in McCain all but being crowned the GOP’s next person to lead the party in the general election.

While the election seemed to be titled in McCain’s favor, it would eventually start to get closer and closer. One point that was brought up is how exactly is McCain a maverick as he likes to say. Was he a maverick from the start or only when it was convenient? These types of attacks were commonplace against the McCain campaign, and the attempts to deal with the damage were not enough. Soon election day came and it saw Al Gore be announced the winner instead of McCain.

", "

The Gore presidency saw a lot done and not a lot done at the same time. Republicans furious at the loss of the election would make attempts at stonewalling his planned agenda, even with the bare majority the Democrats had in the Senate. One piece of legislation the Republicans would block would be Gore’s initiative to push the United States towards a more greener future in investing into renewable energy. This on top of other times the Republicans would block legislation would be a staple of the Gore administration.

Although after 9/11 happened and the Twin Towers were struck down, for a brief time there was unity among the country. Gore’s approval rating soared to as high as 90% at one point, and he would lead the country to war. The war in Afghanistan was met with unanimous praise and approval, but the anti-war base of the Democrats were not happy with the decision. Soon the praise and approval for the president would soon start going down, and the Republicans were all too eager to partake in attacking the president for being too soft.

", "

Now it is 2004 and the Gore presidency is stable, if a bit rocky. Afghanistan seems to be the only thing keeping Gore afloat, but Americans want more blood shed for what happened in 2001. There are numerous people being floated as potential candidates for the Republican primaries. Senator Bond, Mayor Guilaini, and even a comeback for McCain. Whoever the person may be, they will need to do a good job at trying to take the White House.
